# Block Animations | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Source:** [Block Animationsarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/)
 **Last Modified:** Friday, January 9, 2026 at 12:01 PM

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#overview)

Overview


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This guide explains how to add animations to blocks in Hytale. Animations can make your blocks come alive with moving parts, opening mechanisms, or any other dynamic movement.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Basic understanding of block states (see "Block State Changing" guide)
    
*   Blockbench installed ([https://www.blockbench.net/arrow-up-right](https://www.blockbench.net/)
    )
    
*   A block model with named groups
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#what-can-be-animated)

What Can Be Animated?


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Block animations can modify:

*   **Position** - Move elements in X, Y, Z coordinates
    
*   **Orientation** - Rotate elements
    
*   **ShapeStretch** - Stretch or scale elements
    
*   **ShapeVisible** - Show or hide elements
    
*   **ShapeUvOffset** - Animate textures (advanced)
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#step-1-add-animation-to-block-state)

Step 1: Add Animation to Block State


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

First, reference your animation file in the block's state definition:

Copy

    "State": {
      "Definitions": {
        "On": {
          "CustomModelAnimation": "Blocks/Animations/Rising_Water.blockyanim"
        },
        "Off": {
          "CustomModelAnimation": "Blocks/Animations/Empty_Water.blockyanim"
        }
      }
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#step-2-create-groups-in-blockbench)

Step 2: Create Groups in Blockbench


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Open your block model in Blockbench:

1.  **Create a Group:**
    
    *   In Blockbench, create a new group
        
    *   Give it a descriptive name (e.g., "Water", "Door", "Drawer")
        
    *   This group name will be referenced in your animation file
        
    
2.  **Add Elements:**
    
    *   Place the elements you want to animate inside the group
        
    *   You can have multiple elements in one group
        
    *   All elements in the group will animate together
        
    
3.  **Export:**
    
    *   Export as `.blockymodel` format for Hytale
        
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#step-3-create-animation-file)

Step 3: Create Animation File


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Create a `.blockyanim` file in your Pack's animation folder:

**Path:** `YourPackName/Common/Blocks/Animations/Rising_Water.blockyanim`

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#basic-animation-structure)

Basic Animation Structure:

Copy

    {
      "formatVersion": 1,
      "duration": 50,
      "holdLastKeyframe": true,
      "nodeAnimations": {
        "Water": {
          "position": [ /* keyframes */ ],
          "orientation": [ /* keyframes */ ],
          "shapeStretch": [ /* keyframes */ ],
          "shapeVisible": [ /* keyframes */ ],
          "shapeUvOffset": [ /* keyframes */ ]
        }
      }
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#animation-properties)

Animation Properties:

Property

Description

Example

`formatVersion`

Animation format version

`1`

`duration`

Animation length in ticks

`50` (2.5 seconds)

`holdLastKeyframe`

Whether to hold at final position

`true` or `false`

`nodeAnimations`

Object containing group animations

See below

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#animation-types)

Animation Types


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#position-animation)

Position Animation

Moves elements in 3D space:

Copy

    "position": [\
      {\
        "time": 0,\
        "delta": {\
          "x": 0,\
          "y": 0,\
          "z": 0\
        },\
        "interpolationType": "smooth"\
      },\
      {\
        "time": 50,\
        "delta": {\
          "x": 0,\
          "y": 8.5,\
          "z": 0\
        },\
        "interpolationType": "smooth"\
      }\
    ]

**This example:** Moves the element 8.5 units up on the Y-axis over 50 ticks.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#orientation-animation-rotation)

Orientation Animation (Rotation)

Rotates elements using quaternions:

Copy

    "orientation": [\
      {\
        "time": 0,\
        "delta": {\
          "x": 0,\
          "y": 0,\
          "z": 0,\
          "w": 1\
        },\
        "interpolationType": "smooth"\
      },\
      {\
        "time": 15,\
        "delta": {\
          "x": 0,\
          "y": 0.866025,\
          "z": 0,\
          "w": 0.5\
        },\
        "interpolationType": "smooth"\
      }\
    ]

**Note:** Quaternions are complex. Common rotation values:

*   **No rotation:** `{x:0, y:0, z:0, w:1}`
    
*   **90Â° Y-axis:** `{x:0, y:0.707, z:0, w:0.707}`
    
*   **180Â° Y-axis:** `{x:0, y:1, z:0, w:0}`
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#example-1-rising-water-animation)

Example 1: Rising Water Animation


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This animation makes water rise from 0 to 8.5 units upward:

**File:** `Rising_Water.blockyanim`

Copy

    {
      "formatVersion": 1,
      "duration": 50,
      "holdLastKeyframe": true,
      "nodeAnimations": {
        "Water": {
          "position": [\
            {\
              "time": 0,\
              "delta": {\
                "x": 0,\
                "y": 0,\
                "z": 0\
              },\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 50,\
              "delta": {\
                "x": 0,\
                "y": 8.5,\
                "z": 0\
              },\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            }\
          ],
          "orientation": [],
          "shapeStretch": [],
          "shapeVisible": [],
          "shapeUvOffset": []
        }
      }
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#example-2-wardrobe-opening-animation)

Example 2: Wardrobe Opening Animation


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A complex example with multiple animated groups (doors, knockers, drawer):

**File:** `Wardrobe_Open.blockyanim`

Copy

    {
      "formatVersion": 1,
      "duration": 50,
      "holdLastKeyframe": true,
      "nodeAnimations": {
        "Door-L": {
          "position": [],
          "orientation": [\
            {\
              "time": 0,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 0, "w": 1},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 15,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0.866025, "z": 0, "w": 0.5},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 25,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0.793353, "z": 0, "w": 0.608761},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            }\
          ],
          "shapeStretch": [],
          "shapeVisible": [],
          "shapeUvOffset": []
        },
        "Door-R": {
          "position": [],
          "orientation": [\
            {\
              "time": 0,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 0, "w": 1},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 20,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": -0.866025, "z": 0, "w": 0.5},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 30,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": -0.793353, "z": 0, "w": 0.608761},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            }\
          ],
          "shapeStretch": [],
          "shapeVisible": [],
          "shapeUvOffset": []
        },
        "Drawer": {
          "position": [\
            {\
              "time": 0,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 0},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 10,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 12},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 20,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 10},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            }\
          ],
          "orientation": [],
          "shapeStretch": [],
          "shapeVisible": [],
          "shapeUvOffset": []
        },
        "Door-Knocker": {
          "position": [],
          "orientation": [\
            {\
              "time": 0,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 0, "w": 1},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 17,\
              "delta": {"x": -0.5, "y": 0, "z": 0, "w": 0.866025},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 24,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 0, "w": 1},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 32,\
              "delta": {"x": -0.130526, "y": 0, "z": 0, "w": 0.991445},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            },\
            {\
              "time": 40,\
              "delta": {"x": 0, "y": 0, "z": 0, "w": 1},\
              "interpolationType": "smooth"\
            }\
          ],
          "shapeStretch": [],
          "shapeVisible": [],
          "shapeUvOffset": []
        }
      }
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#breakdown-of-wardrobe-animation)

Breakdown of Wardrobe Animation:

*   **Door-L:** Left door swings open (rotates on Y-axis)
    
*   **Door-R:** Right door swings open (opposite direction)
    
*   **Drawer:** Pulls out (moves on Z-axis)
    
*   **Door-Knocker:** Bounces back and forth (multiple rotation keyframes)
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#keyframe-properties)

Keyframe Properties


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each keyframe contains:

Property

Description

`time`

When this keyframe occurs (in ticks)

`delta`

The transformation values

`interpolationType`

How to transition (`"smooth"`, `"linear"`, `"step"`)

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#interpolation-types)

Interpolation Types:

*   **smooth:** Gradual acceleration/deceleration (natural)
    
*   **linear:** Constant speed (mechanical)
    
*   **step:** Instant change (no interpolation)
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#complete-file-structure)

Complete File Structure


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Copy

    YourPackName/
    |-- Common/
    |   `-- Blocks/
    |       |-- Animations/
    |       |   |-- Rising_Water.blockyanim
    |       |   |-- Empty_Water.blockyanim
    |       |   `-- Wardrobe_Open.blockyanim
    |       |-- your_model.blockymodel
    |       `-- Texture/
    |           `-- your_texture.png
    `-- Server/
        `-- Item/
            `-- Items/
                `-- your_block.json

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#tips-for-creating-animations)

Tips for Creating Animations


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Start Simple:** Begin with single-axis position animations
    
2.  **Use Vanilla as Reference:** Look at wardrobe, door, and chest animations
    
3.  **Plan Timing:** Map out when each group should start/stop moving
    
4.  **Test Iteratively:** Test in-game frequently, adjust values
    
5.  **Empty Arrays:** Use `[]` for animation types you don't need
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#testing-your-animations)

Testing Your Animations


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Enable your Pack in a world
    
2.  Place the animated block
    
3.  Trigger the state change (e.g., right-click)
    
4.  Observe the animation
    
5.  Adjust timing and delta values as needed
    
6.  Reload the Pack to see changes
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#troubleshooting)

Troubleshooting


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#animation-doesnt-play)

Animation doesn't play:

*   Verify animation file path in block JSON
    
*   Check that group names match exactly (case-sensitive)
    
*   Ensure `.blockyanim` extension is correct
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#animation-is-choppy)

Animation is choppy:

*   Increase duration for smoother movement
    
*   Use "smooth" interpolation instead of "linear"
    
*   Add more intermediate keyframes
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#wrong-elements-animate)

Wrong elements animate:

*   Check group names in Blockbench
    
*   Verify correct elements are in the group
    
*   Ensure animation references the right group name
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#animation-plays-backwards)

Animation plays backwards:

*   Check time values increase correctly
    
*   Verify keyframes are in chronological order
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#advanced-studying-vanilla-animations)

Advanced: Studying Vanilla Animations


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To learn more, examine vanilla Hytale animations:

**Path:** `Assets/Common/Blocks/Animations/`

Look at:

*   Door animations
    
*   Chest animations
    
*   Wardrobe animations
    
*   Machine animations
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/06-block-animations#credits)

Credits


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Thank you to **Sketch Macaw** for writing this tutorial.

# Gradle Automation & Testing | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Last Modified:** Friday, January 10, 2026

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#overview)

Overview


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This guide covers advanced Gradle automation techniques for Hytale plugin development, including creating custom Gradle tasks for automated server testing and streamlined development workflows.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#custom-gradle-plugin-for-server-testing)

Custom Gradle Plugin for Server Testing


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

One of the most time-consuming parts of plugin development is manually:

1.  Building your plugin
    
2.  Copying it to the server's plugins folder
    
3.  Starting the server
    
4.  Testing your changes
    

You can automate this entire workflow with a custom Gradle plugin!

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#creating-a-custom-gradle-plugin)

Creating a Custom Gradle Plugin


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#project-structure)

Project Structure

Copy

    your-plugin/
    ├── buildSrc/
    │   ├── build.gradle.kts
    │   └── src/
    │       └── main/
    │           └── kotlin/
    │               └── RunHytalePlugin.kt
    ├── build.gradle.kts
    └── src/
        └── main/
            └── java/

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-1-create-buildsrc-directory)

Step 1: Create buildSrc Directory

The `buildSrc/` directory is a special Gradle convention for custom build logic.

Create `buildSrc/build.gradle.kts`:

Copy

    plugins {
        `kotlin-dsl`
    }
    
    repositories {
        mavenCentral()
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-2-create-the-custom-plugin)

Step 2: Create the Custom Plugin

Create `buildSrc/src/main/kotlin/RunHytalePlugin.kt`:

Copy

    import org.gradle.api.DefaultTask
    import org.gradle.api.Plugin
    import org.gradle.api.Project
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.Input
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.TaskAction
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.TaskProvider
    import java.io.File
    import java.net.URI
    import java.security.MessageDigest
    
    // Main plugin class
    open class RunHytalePlugin : Plugin<Project> {
        override fun apply(project: Project) {
            // Create extension for configuration
            val extension = project.extensions.create(
                "runHytale", 
                RunHytaleExtension::class.java
            )
    
            // Register the runServer task
            val runTask: TaskProvider<RunServerTask> = project.tasks.register(
                "runServer", 
                RunServerTask::class.java
            ) {
                jarUrl.set(extension.jarUrl)
                group = "hytale"
                description = "Downloads and runs the Hytale server with your plugin"
            }
    
            // Make runServer depend on shadowJar (build plugin first)
            project.tasks.findByName("shadowJar")?.let {
                runTask.configure {
                    dependsOn(it)
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Extension for configuration
    open class RunHytaleExtension {
        var jarUrl: String = "https://example.com/hytale-server.jar"
    }
    
    // The actual task that runs the server
    open class RunServerTask : DefaultTask() {
    
        @Input
        val jarUrl = project.objects.property(String::class.java)
    
        @TaskAction
        fun run() {
            // Create directories
            val runDir = File(project.projectDir, "run").apply { mkdirs() }
            val pluginsDir = File(runDir, "plugins").apply { mkdirs() }
            val jarFile = File(runDir, "server.jar")
    
            // Cache directory for downloaded server JARs
            val cacheDir = File(
                project.layout.buildDirectory.asFile.get(), 
                "hytale-cache"
            ).apply { mkdirs() }
    
            // Compute hash of URL for caching
            val urlHash = MessageDigest.getInstance("SHA-256")
                .digest(jarUrl.get().toByteArray())
                .joinToString("") { "%02x".format(it) }
            val cachedJar = File(cacheDir, "$urlHash.jar")
    
            // Download server JAR if not cached
            if (!cachedJar.exists()) {
                println("Downloading Hytale server from ${jarUrl.get()}")
                URI.create(jarUrl.get()).toURL().openStream().use { input ->
                    cachedJar.outputStream().use { output ->
                        input.copyTo(output)
                    }
                }
                println("Server JAR downloaded and cached")
            } else {
                println("Using cached server JAR")
            }
    
            // Copy server JAR to run directory
            cachedJar.copyTo(jarFile, overwrite = true)
    
            // Copy plugin JAR to plugins folder
            project.tasks.findByName("shadowJar")?.outputs?.files?.firstOrNull()?.let { shadowJar ->
                val targetFile = File(pluginsDir, shadowJar.name)
                shadowJar.copyTo(targetFile, overwrite = true)
                println("Plugin copied to: ${targetFile.absolutePath}")
            }
    
            println("Starting Hytale server...")
    
            // Start the server process
            val process = ProcessBuilder("java", "-jar", jarFile.name)
                .directory(runDir)
                .start()
    
            // Handle graceful shutdown
            project.gradle.buildFinished {
                if (process.isAlive) {
                    println("Stopping server...")
                    process.destroy()
                }
            }
    
            // Forward stdout to console
            Thread {
                process.inputStream.bufferedReader().useLines { lines ->
                    lines.forEach { println(it) }
                }
            }.start()
    
            // Forward stderr to console
            Thread {
                process.errorStream.bufferedReader().useLines { lines ->
                    lines.forEach { System.err.println(it) }
                }
            }.start()
    
            // Forward stdin to server (for commands)
            Thread {
                System.`in`.bufferedReader().useLines { lines ->
                    lines.forEach {
                        process.outputStream.write((it + "\n").toByteArray())
                        process.outputStream.flush()
                    }
                }
            }.start()
    
            // Wait for server to exit
            val exitCode = process.waitFor()
            println("Server exited with code $exitCode")
        }
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-3-apply-the-plugin)

Step 3: Apply the Plugin

In your main `build.gradle.kts`:

Copy

    plugins {
        id("java")
        id("com.gradleup.shadow") version "9.3.1"
        id("run-hytale") // Your custom plugin
    }
    
    // Configure the plugin
    runHytale {
        jarUrl = "https://example.com/hytale-server.jar" // Replace with actual URL
    }
    
    // Rest of your build configuration...

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#step-4-use-the-task)

Step 4: Use the Task

Copy

    # Build and run server with your plugin
    ./gradlew runServer
    
    # On Windows:
    gradlew.bat runServer

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#how-it-works)

How It Works


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-1.-smart-caching)

1\. **Smart Caching**

*   Downloads server JAR only once
    
*   Uses SHA-256 hash of URL as cache key
    
*   Subsequent runs use cached version
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-2.-automatic-build)

2\. **Automatic Build**

*   Depends on `shadowJar` task
    
*   Builds your plugin before running
    
*   Copies fresh plugin JAR to server
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-3.-interactive-console)

3\. **Interactive Console**

*   Forwards server output to your terminal
    
*   Allows typing commands directly
    
*   Handles Ctrl+C gracefully
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-4.-clean-workspace)

4\. **Clean Workspace**

*   Server runs in `run/` directory
    
*   Keeps your project root clean
    
*   Easy to delete and reset
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#advanced-gradle-tasks)

Advanced Gradle Tasks


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#auto-reload-development-task)

Auto-Reload Development Task

Create a task that watches for changes and auto-reloads:

Copy

    // In buildSrc/src/main/kotlin/DevModeTask.kt
    import org.gradle.api.DefaultTask
    import org.gradle.api.tasks.TaskAction
    import java.nio.file.*
    
    open class DevModeTask : DefaultTask() {
        
        @TaskAction
        fun run() {
            val watchService = FileSystems.getDefault().newWatchService()
            val srcPath = project.file("src/main/java").toPath()
            
            srcPath.register(
                watchService,
                StandardWatchEventKinds.ENTRY_MODIFY,
                StandardWatchEventKinds.ENTRY_CREATE
            )
            
            println("Watching for changes in src/main/java...")
            println("Press Ctrl+C to stop")
            
            while (true) {
                val key = watchService.take()
                
                for (event in key.pollEvents()) {
                    println("Change detected: ${event.context()}")
                    println("Rebuilding plugin...")
                    
                    // Trigger rebuild
                    project.tasks.findByName("shadowJar")?.actions?.forEach { 
                        it.execute(project.tasks.getByName("shadowJar"))
                    }
                    
                    println("Rebuild complete. Copy to server and reload.")
                }
                
                key.reset()
            }
        }
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#quick-test-task)

Quick Test Task

Create a task for quick compilation checks:

Copy

    tasks.register("quickTest") {
        group = "verification"
        description = "Quick compilation and basic checks"
        
        dependsOn("compileJava")
        
        doLast {
            println("✓ Compilation successful")
            println("✓ No syntax errors")
            
            // Check manifest exists
            val manifest = file("src/main/resources/manifest.json")
            if (manifest.exists()) {
                println("✓ Manifest file found")
            } else {
                throw GradleException("✗ Manifest file missing!")
            }
            
            // Check for common issues
            val srcDir = file("src/main/java")
            srcDir.walk().forEach { file ->
                if (file.extension == "java") {
                    val content = file.readText()
                    
                    // Check for System.out.println (should use logger)
                    if (content.contains("System.out.println")) {
                        println("⚠ Warning: Found System.out.println in ${file.name}")
                        println("  Consider using a logger instead")
                    }
                }
            }
            
            println("\n✓ Quick test passed!")
        }
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#gradle-build-optimizations)

Gradle Build Optimizations


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#enable-gradle-daemon)

Enable Gradle Daemon

Add to `gradle.properties`:

Copy

    # Enable daemon for faster builds
    org.gradle.daemon=true
    
    # Increase memory for large projects
    org.gradle.jvmargs=-Xmx2048m -XX:MaxMetaspaceSize=512m
    
    # Enable parallel builds
    org.gradle.parallel=true
    
    # Enable build cache
    org.gradle.caching=true
    
    # Use configuration cache (Gradle 8+)
    org.gradle.configuration-cache=true

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#optimize-shadowjar-task)

Optimize ShadowJar Task

Copy

    tasks.shadowJar {
        // Minimize JAR size
        minimize()
        
        // Relocate dependencies to avoid conflicts
        relocate("com.google.gson", "com.yourplugin.libs.gson")
        
        // Exclude unnecessary files
        exclude("META-INF/*.SF")
        exclude("META-INF/*.DSA")
        exclude("META-INF/*.RSA")
        
        // Set archive name
        archiveBaseName.set("YourPlugin")
        archiveClassifier.set("")
        archiveVersion.set(project.version.toString())
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#multi-environment-testing)

Multi-Environment Testing


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#test-against-multiple-server-versions)

Test Against Multiple Server Versions

Copy

    // In build.gradle.kts
    val serverVersions = mapOf(
        "latest" to "https://example.com/hytale-latest.jar",
        "stable" to "https://example.com/hytale-stable.jar",
        "beta" to "https://example.com/hytale-beta.jar"
    )
    
    serverVersions.forEach { (name, url) ->
        tasks.register("runServer-$name", RunServerTask::class) {
            group = "hytale"
            description = "Run server with $name version"
            jarUrl.set(url)
        }
    }
    
    // Usage:
    // ./gradlew runServer-latest
    // ./gradlew runServer-stable
    // ./gradlew runServer-beta

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#continuous-integration)

Continuous Integration


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#github-actions-workflow)

GitHub Actions Workflow

Create `.github/workflows/build.yml`:

Copy

    name: Build Plugin
    
    on:
      push:
        branches: [ main, develop ]
      pull_request:
        branches: [ main ]
    
    jobs:
      build:
        runs-on: ubuntu-latest
        
        steps:
        - uses: actions/checkout@v3
        
        - name: Set up JDK 25
          uses: actions/setup-java@v3
          with:
            java-version: '25'
            distribution: 'temurin'
        
        - name: Grant execute permission for gradlew
          run: chmod +x gradlew
        
        - name: Build with Gradle
          run: ./gradlew build
        
        - name: Run tests
          run: ./gradlew test
        
        - name: Upload artifact
          uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
          with:
            name: plugin-jar
            path: build/libs/*.jar

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#debugging-with-gradle)

Debugging with Gradle


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#enable-debug-mode)

Enable Debug Mode

Copy

    # Run with debug output
    ./gradlew runServer --debug
    
    # Run with info output
    ./gradlew runServer --info
    
    # Run with stack traces
    ./gradlew runServer --stacktrace

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#remote-debugging)

Remote Debugging

Modify the RunServerTask to support remote debugging:

Copy

    // Add debug flag
    val debugMode = project.hasProperty("debug")
    
    val javaArgs = mutableListOf("-jar", jarFile.name)
    if (debugMode) {
        javaArgs.add(0, "-agentlib:jdwp=transport=dt_socket,server=y,suspend=n,address=5005")
        println("Debug mode enabled. Connect debugger to port 5005")
    }
    
    val process = ProcessBuilder("java", *javaArgs.toTypedArray())
        .directory(runDir)
        .start()

Usage:

Copy

    ./gradlew runServer -Pdebug

Then connect your IDE debugger to `localhost:5005`.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#best-practices)

Best Practices


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-1.-version-control)

1\. **Version Control**

Copy

    # .gitignore
    build/
    run/
    .gradle/
    *.jar
    !gradle-wrapper.jar

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-2.-clean-task)

2\. **Clean Task**

Copy

    tasks.register("cleanRun") {
        group = "hytale"
        description = "Clean run directory"
        
        doLast {
            delete("run")
            println("Run directory cleaned")
        }
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#id-3.-dependency-management)

3\. **Dependency Management**

Copy

    dependencies {
        // Use compileOnly for server dependencies
        compileOnly(files("libs/hytale-server.jar"))
        
        // Use implementation for bundled dependencies
        implementation("com.google.code.gson:gson:2.10.1")
        
        // Use testImplementation for test dependencies
        testImplementation("org.junit.jupiter:junit-jupiter:5.10.0")
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#troubleshooting)

Troubleshooting


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/13-gradle-automation-testing#common-issues)

Common Issues

**Issue: Server JAR not downloading**

Copy

    // Add timeout and retry logic
    val connection = URI.create(jarUrl.get()).toURL().openConnection()
    connection.connectTimeout = 30000
    connection.readTimeout = 30000

**Issue: Plugin not copying**

Copy

    // Verify shadowJar output
    tasks.shadowJar {
        doLast {
            println("Plugin JAR created: ${archiveFile.get().asFile.absolutePath}")
        }
    }

**Issue: Server not starting**

Copy

    # Check Java version
    java -version
    
    # Check server JAR is valid
    java -jar run/server.jar --version

*   **Faster Development**: One command to build, deploy, and test

# Getting Started with Plugins | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Source:** [Getting Started with Pluginsarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/)
 **Last Modified:** Friday, January 9, 2026 at 12:09 PM

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#overview)

Overview


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This guide will help you get started with creating **Plugins** for Hytale. Plugins are mods written in **Java** that use the game's API to expand vanilla functionality and add new content programmatically.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Before you begin, ensure you have:

*   **Hytale** installed via the official launcher
    
*   **IntelliJ IDEA** (Community Edition is fine)
    
*   **Java 25** downloaded and configured
    
*   Basic **Java programming** knowledge
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-1-download-the-idea-template)

Step 1: Download the IDEA Template


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The easiest way to start developing plugins is by using the official template created by **Darkhax & Jared**.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#download-options)

Download Options:

*   **Zip File:** (Link TBC - Check Community documentation)
    
*   **GitHub Repo:** (Link TBC - Check Community documentation)
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#template-features)

Template Features:

The template includes many great features:

*   Adds the latest Hytale server files to your classpath
    
*   Run the game from your IDE with breakpoint support
    
*   Bundle assets with your plugin (editable with in-game Asset Editor)
    
*   Supports various patch lines (releases and pre-releases)
    
*   Includes example code and assets
    
*   Pre-configured Gradle build system
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-2-setup-the-template)

Step 2: Setup the Template


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-2.1-extract-the-template)

2.1 Extract the Template

1.  Download the ZIP file
    
2.  Extract contents to your desired development location
    
3.  Read the included `README.md` for detailed setup instructions
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-2.2-complete-prerequisites-checklist)

2.2 Complete Prerequisites Checklist

Ensure you have completed all the following before proceeding:

#### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#prerequisites-checklist)

Prerequisites Checklist:

1.  **Download Hytale** using the official launcher
    
2.  **Install IntelliJ IDEA** (Community Edition is sufficient)
    
3.  **Download Java 25** and add it as an SDK in IDEA
    
4.  **Set your project name** in `settings.gradle`
    
5.  **Review the properties** in `gradle.properties`
    
6.  **Update the manifest** in `src/main/resources/manifest.json`
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-3-configure-your-project)

Step 3: Configure Your Project


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-3.1-set-project-name)

3.1 Set Project Name

Edit `settings.gradle`:

Copy

    rootProject.name = 'your-plugin-name'

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-3.2-review-gradle-properties)

3.2 Review Gradle Properties

Open and review `gradle.properties`:

Copy

    # Example properties (actual values may vary)
    hytale_version=latest
    plugin_version=1.0.0
    # ... other properties

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-3.3-update-manifest-file)

3.3 Update Manifest File

Edit `src/main/resources/manifest.json` with your project information:

Copy

    {
      "Group": "com.yourname",
      "Name": "YourPluginName",
      "Version": "1.0.0",
      "Description": "Description of your plugin",
      "Authors": [\
        {\
          "Name": "Your Name",\
          "Email": "your.email@example.com",\
          "Url": "https://your-website.com"\
        }\
      ],
      "Website": "https://your-plugin-website.com",
      "ServerVersion": "*",
      "Dependencies": {},
      "OptionalDependencies": {},
      "DisabledByDefault": false
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-4-open-the-project-in-idea)

Step 4: Open the Project in IDEA


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Launch IntelliJ IDEA**
    
2.  **Open Project:**
    
    *   Click `File` –†’ `Open`
        
    *   Navigate to your extracted template folder
        
    *   Select the folder and click `OK`
        
    
3.  **Wait for Initialization:**
    
    *   IDEA will import the Gradle project
        
    *   Dependencies will be downloaded automatically
        
    *   This may take several minutes on first run
        
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-5-configure-java-25-sdk)

Step 5: Configure Java 25 SDK


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you haven't already added Java 25 as an SDK:

1.  **Open Project Structure:**
    
    *   `File` –†’ `Project Structure` (or `Ctrl+Alt+Shift+S`)
        
    
2.  **Add SDK:**
    
    *   Click `SDKs` under `Platform Settings`
        
    *   Click `+` –†’ `Add JDK`
        
    *   Navigate to your Java 25 installation
        
    *   Click `OK`
        
    
3.  **Set Project SDK:**
    
    *   Go to `Project` settings
        
    *   Set `SDK` to Java 25
        
    *   Click `Apply` and `OK`
        
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-6-understanding-the-project-structure)

Step 6: Understanding the Project Structure


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Copy

    your-plugin-name/
    |-- src/
    |   `-- main/
    |       |-- java/
    |       |   `-- com/
    |       |       `-- yourname/
    |       |           `-- yourplugin/
    |       |               `-- YourPlugin.java
    |       `-- resources/
    |           |-- manifest.json
    |           |-- Common/          # Assets (models, textures)
    |           `-- Server/          # Server-side data
    |-- build.gradle
    |-- settings.gradle
    |-- gradle.properties
    `-- README.md

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-7-running-the-game-from-idea)

Step 7: Running the Game from IDEA


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#pre-configured-run-configuration)

Pre-configured Run Configuration

The template includes a run configuration called **HytaleServer**:

1.  **Select Run Configuration:**
    
    *   Look for the dropdown in the top-right of IDEA
        
    *   Select `HytaleServer`
        
    
2.  **Run or Debug:**
    
    *   Click the green play button to run
        
    *   Click the bug button to debug with breakpoints
        
    
3.  **Game Launches:**
    
    *   Hytale will start with your plugin loaded
        
    *   You can set breakpoints in your code
        
    *   Debug console shows plugin output
        
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-8-building-your-plugin)

Step 8: Building Your Plugin


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To create a shareable JAR file of your plugin:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#build-with-gradle)

Build with Gradle:

**Option 1: Terminal**

Copy

    ./gradlew build

**Option 2: IDEA Gradle Panel**

1.  Open the Gradle panel (right side of IDEA)
    
2.  Navigate to: `Tasks` –†’ `build` –†’ `build`
    
3.  Double-click `build`
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#output-location)

Output Location:

Your plugin JAR will be in:

Copy

    build/libs/your-plugin-name-1.0.0.jar

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#step-9-installing-plugins)

Step 9: Installing Plugins


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To install plugins in Hytale:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#installation-path)

Installation Path:

Copy

    %appdata%/Hytale/UserData/Mods/

**Full Path (Windows):**

Copy

    C:\Users\YourUsername\AppData\Roaming\Hytale\UserData\Mods\

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#installation-steps)

Installation Steps:

1.  **Create Mods Folder** (if it doesn't exist)
    
2.  **Copy your plugin JAR** into the `Mods/` folder
    
3.  **Launch Hytale**
    
4.  Your plugin will be loaded automatically
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#example-plugin-code)

Example Plugin Code


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here's a basic plugin structure:

Copy

    package com.yourname.yourplugin;
    
    import com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.JavaPlugin;
    import com.hypixel.hytale.plugin.JavaPluginInit;
    import javax.annotation.Nonnull;
    
    public class YourPlugin extends JavaPlugin {
    
        public YourPlugin(@Nonnull JavaPluginInit init) {
            super(init);
            
            // Plugin initialization code
            getLogger().info("YourPlugin has been loaded!");
        }
    
        @Override
        public void onEnable() {
            // Called when plugin is enabled
            getLogger().info("YourPlugin enabled!");
        }
    
        @Override
        public void onDisable() {
            // Called when plugin is disabled
            getLogger().info("YourPlugin disabled!");
        }
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#plugin-development-tips)

Plugin Development Tips


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-1.-use-the-logger)

1\. Use the Logger

Copy

    getLogger().info("Information message");
    getLogger().warn("Warning message");
    getLogger().error("Error message");

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-2.-register-event-listeners)

2\. Register Event Listeners

Copy

    getServer().getPluginManager().registerEvents(new MyListener(), this);

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-3.-access-the-api)

3\. Access the API

The template includes Hytale's API in the classpath:

*   Explore the API through IntelliJ's autocomplete
    
*   Check the example code included in the template
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#id-4.-bundle-assets)

4\. Bundle Assets

You can include Packs (assets) with your Plugin:

*   Add assets to `src/main/resources/Common/` and `Server/`
    
*   They'll be bundled with your plugin JAR
    
*   Editable in-game via the Asset Editor
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#debugging-tips)

Debugging Tips


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#breakpoints)

Breakpoints

1.  Click in the left margin next to a line number
    
2.  A red dot appears indicating a breakpoint
    
3.  Run in Debug mode
    
4.  Execution pauses at breakpoints
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#console-output)

Console Output

*   Plugin logs appear in the IDEA console
    
*   Use `getLogger()` for clean output
    
*   Check for error stack traces
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#hot-reload)

Hot Reload

*   Some changes can be reloaded without restarting
    
*   Rebuild the project (`Ctrl+F9`)
    
*   Major changes require a full restart
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#next-steps)

Next Steps


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

After setting up your plugin development environment:

1.  **Explore the API** - Browse available classes and methods
    
2.  **Read Example Code** - Study the included examples
    
3.  **Create Custom Features** - Start implementing your ideas
    
4.  **Use Config Files** - See "Custom Config Files" tutorial
    
5.  **Advanced Modding** - Explore "Bootstrap/Early Plugins" if needed
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#troubleshooting)

Troubleshooting


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#gradle-sync-fails)

Gradle sync fails:

*   Check internet connection (downloads dependencies)
    
*   Verify Java 25 is properly installed
    
*   Try: `./gradlew clean build`
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#hytaleserver-run-config-missing)

HytaleServer run config missing:

*   Re-import Gradle project
    
*   Check `build.gradle` for run configuration setup
    
*   Manually create run configuration if needed
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#plugin-doesnt-load)

Plugin doesn't load:

*   Verify manifest.json is correct
    
*   Check logs for error messages
    
*   Ensure plugin JAR is in correct Mods folder
    
*   Confirm Hytale version compatibility
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#breakpoints-dont-work)

Breakpoints don't work:

*   Ensure you're running in Debug mode (bug icon)
    
*   Verify breakpoint is in executed code
    
*   Check that source code matches compiled JAR
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/plugins-java-development/07-getting-started-with-plugins#additional-resources)

# Block State Changing | Hytale Modding Documentation

**Source:** [Block State Changingarrow-up-right](https://hytale.com/)
 **Last Modified:** Friday, January 9, 2026 at 12:01 PM

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#overview)

Overview


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This is a basic beginner's guide on how to modify block state changes and cycling. Block states allow you to create blocks that can change appearance, behavior, or properties when interacted with, similar to doors, lights, or buttons in the game.

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#what-are-block-states)

What are Block States?


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Block states allow a single block to have multiple configurations or modes:

*   **Lamps** that can be on or off
    
*   **Doors** that can be open or closed
    
*   **Machines** that can be active or inactive
    
*   **Any block** with multiple visual or functional states
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#step-1-select-your-block)

Step 1: Select Your Block


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

First, locate your block definition file:

**Path:** `Packs/YourPackName/Server/Item/Items/your_block.json`

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#step-2-create-an-interaction)

Step 2: Create an Interaction


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Define an interaction that will trigger the state change. This tells the game what should happen when the player interacts with the block.

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#interaction-structure)

Interaction Structure:

Copy

    "Interactions": {
      "Use": {
        "Interactions": [\
          {\
            "Type": "ChangeState",\
            "Changes": {\
              "default": "Off",\
              "On": "Off",\
              "Off": "On"\
            }\
          }\
        ]
      }
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#interaction-properties-explained)

Interaction Properties Explained:

Property

Description

`"Use"`

The interaction type (player right-clicks/uses the block)

`"Type": "ChangeState"`

Tells the game to change the block's state

`"Changes"`

Maps current state –†’ next state

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#state-cycling-logic)

State Cycling Logic:

Copy

    "Changes": {
      "default": "Off",  // Initial state when placed
      "On": "Off",       // When "On", change to "Off"
      "Off": "On"        // When "Off", change to "On"
    }

This creates a toggle behavior: On –†’ Off –†’ On –†’ Off...

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#step-3-define-states)

Step 3: Define States


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Now define what each state looks like and behaves like:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#state-definition-structure)

State Definition Structure:

Copy

    "State": {
      "Definitions": {
        "On": {
          "InteractionHint": "interactionHints.turnoff",
          "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_one.blockymodel",
          "CustomModelTexture": [\
            {\
              "Texture": "Blocks/Texture/textureone.png"\
            }\
          ]
        },
        "Off": {
          "InteractionHint": "interactionHints.turnon",
          "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_two.blockymodel",
          "CustomModelTexture": [\
            {\
              "Texture": "Blocks/Texture/textureone.png"\
            }\
          ]
        }
      }
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#state-properties)

State Properties:

Property

Description

Example

`InteractionHint`

Tooltip shown when hovering

`"interactionHints.turnoff"`

`CustomModel`

Model file for this state

`"Blocks/model_one.blockymodel"`

`CustomModelTexture`

Texture(s) for this state

Array of texture objects

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#complete-example-block)

Complete Example Block


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Here's a full example of a block with state changing:

Copy

    {
      "TranslationProperties": {
        "Name": "server.Toggle_Block.name"
      },
      "MaxStack": 100,
      "Icon": "Icons/ItemsGenerated/Toggle_Block.png",
      "Categories": [\
        "Blocks.Decoration"\
      ],
      "BlockType": {
        "DrawType": "Model",
        "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_one.blockymodel",
        "CustomModelTexture": [\
          {\
            "Texture": "Blocks/your_texture.png"\
          }\
        ],
        
        "Interactions": {
          "Use": {
            "Interactions": [\
              {\
                "Type": "ChangeState",\
                "Changes": {\
                  "default": "Off",\
                  "On": "Off",\
                  "Off": "On"\
                }\
              }\
            ]
          }
        },
        
        "State": {
          "Definitions": {
            "On": {
              "InteractionHint": "interactionHints.turnoff",
              "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_one.blockymodel",
              "CustomModelTexture": [\
                {\
                  "Texture": "Blocks/Texture/textureone.png"\
                }\
              ]
            },
            "Off": {
              "InteractionHint": "interactionHints.turnon",
              "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_two.blockymodel",
              "CustomModelTexture": [\
                {\
                  "Texture": "Blocks/Texture/textureone.png"\
                }\
              ]
            }
          }
        }
      }
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#advanced-state-features)

Advanced State Features


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can add additional properties to each state:

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#sounds)

Sounds

Copy

    "On": {
      "InteractionHint": "interactionHints.turnoff",
      "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_one.blockymodel",
      "BlockSoundSetId": "Metal_On"
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#animations)

Animations

Copy

    "On": {
      "InteractionHint": "interactionHints.turnoff",
      "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_one.blockymodel",
      "CustomModelAnimation": "Blocks/Animations/Light_On.blockyanim"
    }

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#particles)

Particles

Copy

    "On": {
      "InteractionHint": "interactionHints.turnoff",
      "CustomModel": "Blocks/model_one.blockymodel",
      "ParticleColor": "#ffff00"
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#multiple-states-beyond-on-off)

Multiple States (Beyond On/Off)


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can have more than two states:

Copy

    "Interactions": {
      "Use": {
        "Interactions": [\
          {\
            "Type": "ChangeState",\
            "Changes": {\
              "default": "State1",\
              "State1": "State2",\
              "State2": "State3",\
              "State3": "State1"\
            }\
          }\
        ]
      }
    }

Then define all three states:

Copy

    "State": {
      "Definitions": {
        "State1": { /* ... */ },
        "State2": { /* ... */ },
        "State3": { /* ... */ }
      }
    }

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#interaction-hints-translation)

Interaction Hints Translation


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Remember to add translations for your interaction hints:

**Path:** `YourPackName/Server/Languages/en-US/interactionHints.lang`

Copy

    turnon = Turn On
    turnoff = Turn Off

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#required-files)

Required Files


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For a state-changing block with custom models, you need:

Copy

    YourPackName/
    |-- Common/
    |   `-- Blocks/
    |       |-- model_one.blockymodel
    |       |-- model_two.blockymodel
    |       `-- Texture/
    |           `-- textureone.png
    `-- Server/
        |-- Item/
        |   `-- Items/
        |       `-- your_block.json
        `-- Languages/
            `-- en-US/
                `-- interactionHints.lang

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#testing-your-state-changing-block)

Testing Your State-Changing Block


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Enable your Pack in a world
    
2.  Place the block
    
3.  Observe its initial state (default)
    
4.  Right-click/use the block
    
5.  Verify it changes to the next state
    
6.  Check that the model/texture updates
    
7.  Verify the interaction hint displays correctly
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#troubleshooting)

Troubleshooting


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#states-dont-change)

States don't change:

*   Verify `"Type": "ChangeState"` is set correctly
    
*   Check that state names match in `Changes` and `Definitions`
    
*   Ensure interaction type is correct (`"Use"`)
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#wrong-initial-state)

Wrong initial state:

*   Check `"default"` value in `Changes`
    
*   Verify the default state is defined in `Definitions`
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#models-textures-dont-update)

Models/textures don't update:

*   Verify model paths are correct for each state
    
*   Check that texture paths exist
    
*   Ensure models are properly formatted `.blockymodel` files
    

### 

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#interaction-hints-dont-show)

Interaction hints don't show:

*   Verify translation keys exist in `interactionHints.lang`
    
*   Check that language file is in correct location
    
*   Ensure no typos in translation keys
    

* * *

[hashtag](https://britakee-studios.gitbook.io/hytale-modding-documentation/packs-content-creation/04-block-state-changing#credits)

Credits


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Thank you to **Sketch Macaw** for helping to write this article!
